     1	/*
     2	 * Index-based KV store implementation
     3	 * This file implements a KV store comprised of an array of dicts (see dict.c)
     4	 * The purpose of this KV store is to have easy access to all keys that belong
     5	 * in the same dict (i.e. are in the same dict-index)
     6	 *
     7	 * For example, when Redis is running in cluster mode, we use kvstore to save
     8	 * all keys that map to the same hash-slot in a separate dict within the kvstore
     9	 * struct.
    10	 * This enables us to easily access all keys that map to a specific hash-slot.
    11	 *
    12	 * Copyright (c) 2011-Present, Redis Ltd. and contributors.
    13	 * All rights reserved.
    14	 *
    15	 * Copyright (c) 2024-present, Valkey contributors.
    16	 * All rights reserved.
    17	 *
    18	 * Licensed under your choice of (a) the Redis Source Available License 2.0
    19	 * (RSALv2); or (b) the Server Side Public License v1 (SSPLv1); or (c) the
    20	 * GNU Affero General Public License v3 (AGPLv3).
    21	 *
    22	 * Portions of this file are available under BSD3 terms; see REDISCONTRIBUTIONS for more information.
    23	 */
    24	
    25	#include "fmacros.h"
    26	
    27	#include <string.h>
    28	#include <stddef.h>
    29	
    30	#include "zmalloc.h"
    31	#include "kvstore.h"
    32	#include "redisassert.h"
    33	#include "monotonic.h"
    34	
    35	#define UNUSED(V) ((void) V)
    36	
    37	struct _kvstore {
    38	    int flags;
    39	    dictType dtype;
    40	    dict **dicts;
    41	    long long num_dicts;
    42	    long long num_dicts_bits;
    43	    list *rehashing;                       /* List of dictionaries in this kvstore that are currently rehashing. */
    44	    int resize_cursor;                     /* Cron job uses this cursor to gradually resize dictionaries (only used if num_dicts > 1). */
    45	    int allocated_dicts;                   /* The number of allocated dicts. */
    46	    int non_empty_dicts;                   /* The number of non-empty dicts. */
    47	    unsigned long long key_count;          /* Total number of keys in this kvstore. */
    48	    unsigned long long bucket_count;       /* Total number of buckets in this kvstore across dictionaries. */
    49	    unsigned long long *dict_size_index;   /* Binary indexed tree (BIT) that describes cumulative key frequencies up until given dict-index. */
    50	    size_t overhead_hashtable_rehashing;   /* The overhead of dictionaries rehashing. */
    51	    void *metadata[];                      /* conditionally allocated based on "flags" */
    52	};
    53	
    54	/* Structure for kvstore iterator that allows iterating across multiple dicts. */
    55	struct _kvstoreIterator {
    56	    kvstore *kvs;
    57	    long long didx;
    58	    long long next_didx;
    59	    dictIterator di;
    60	};
    61	
    62	/* Structure for kvstore dict iterator that allows iterating the corresponding dict. */
    63	struct _kvstoreDictIterator {
    64	    kvstore *kvs;
    65	    long long didx;
    66	    dictIterator di;
    67	};
    68	
    69	/* Basic metadata allocated per dict */
    70	typedef struct {
    71	    listNode *rehashing_node;   /* list node in rehashing list */
    72	} kvstoreDictMetaBase;
    73	
    74	/* Conditionally metadata allocated per dict (specifically for keysizes histogram) */
    75	typedef struct {
    76	    kvstoreDictMetaBase base; /* must be first in struct ! */
    77	    /* External metadata */
    78	    kvstoreDictMetadata meta;
    79	} kvstoreDictMetaEx;
    80	
    81	/**********************************/
    82	/*** Helpers **********************/
    83	/**********************************/
    84	
    85	/* Get the dictionary pointer based on dict-index. */
    86	dict *kvstoreGetDict(kvstore *kvs, int didx) {
    87	    return kvs->dicts[didx];
    88	}
    89	
    90	static dict **kvstoreGetDictRef(kvstore *kvs, int didx) {
    91	    return &kvs->dicts[didx];
    92	}
    93	
    94	static int kvstoreDictIsRehashingPaused(kvstore *kvs, int didx)
    95	{
    96	    dict *d = kvstoreGetDict(kvs, didx);
    97	    return d ? dictIsRehashingPaused(d) : 0;
    98	}
    99	
   100	/* Returns total (cumulative) number of keys up until given dict-index (inclusive).
   101	 * Time complexity is O(log(kvs->num_dicts)). */
   102	static unsigned long long cumulativeKeyCountRead(kvstore *kvs, int didx) {
   103	    if (kvs->num_dicts == 1) {
   104	        assert(didx == 0);
   105	        return kvstoreSize(kvs);
   106	    }
   107	    int idx = didx + 1;
   108	    unsigned long long sum = 0;
   109	    while (idx > 0) {
   110	        sum += kvs->dict_size_index[idx];
   111	        idx -= (idx & -idx);
   112	    }
   113	    return sum;
   114	}
   115	
   116	static void addDictIndexToCursor(kvstore *kvs, int didx, unsigned long long *cursor) {
   117	    if (kvs->num_dicts == 1)
   118	        return;
   119	    /* didx can be -1 when iteration is over and there are no more dicts to visit. */
   120	    if (didx < 0)
   121	        return;
   122	    *cursor = (*cursor << kvs->num_dicts_bits) | didx;
   123	}
   124	
   125	static int getAndClearDictIndexFromCursor(kvstore *kvs, unsigned long long *cursor) {
   126	    if (kvs->num_dicts == 1)
   127	        return 0;
   128	    int didx = (int) (*cursor & (kvs->num_dicts-1));
   129	    *cursor = *cursor >> kvs->num_dicts_bits;
   130	    return didx;
   131	}
   132	
   133	/* Updates binary index tree (also known as Fenwick tree), increasing key count for a given dict.
   134	 * You can read more about this data structure here https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fenwick_tree
   135	 * Time complexity is O(log(kvs->num_dicts)). Take care to call it only after 
   136	 * adding or removing keys from the kvstore.
   137	 */
   138	static void cumulativeKeyCountAdd(kvstore *kvs, int didx, long delta) {
   139	    kvs->key_count += delta;
   140	
   141	    dict *d = kvstoreGetDict(kvs, didx);
   142	    size_t dsize = dictSize(d);
   143	    /* Increment if dsize is 1 and delta is positive (first element inserted, dict becomes non-empty).
   144	     * Decrement if dsize is 0 (dict becomes empty). */
   145	    int non_empty_dicts_delta = (dsize == 1 && delta > 0) ? 1 : (dsize == 0) ? -1 : 0;
   146	    kvs->non_empty_dicts += non_empty_dicts_delta;
   147	
   148	    /* BIT does not need to be calculated when there's only one dict. */
   149	    if (kvs->num_dicts == 1)
   150	        return;
   151	
   152	    /* Update the BIT */
   153	    int idx = didx + 1; /* Unlike dict indices, BIT is 1-based, so we need to add 1. */
   154	    while (idx <= kvs->num_dicts) {
   155	        if (delta < 0) {
   156	            assert(kvs->dict_size_index[idx] >= (unsigned long long)labs(delta));
   157	        }
   158	        kvs->dict_size_index[idx] += delta;
   159	        idx += (idx & -idx);
   160	    }
   161	}
   162	
   163	/* Create the dict if it does not exist and return it. */
   164	static dict *createDictIfNeeded(kvstore *kvs, int didx) {
   165	    dict *d = kvstoreGetDict(kvs, didx);
   166	    if (d) return d;
   167	
   168	    kvs->dicts[didx] = dictCreate(&kvs->dtype);
   169	    kvs->allocated_dicts++;
   170	    return kvs->dicts[didx];
   171	}
   172	
   173	/* Called when the dict will delete entries, the function will check
   174	 * KVSTORE_FREE_EMPTY_DICTS to determine whether the empty dict needs
   175	 * to be freed.
   176	 *
   177	 * Note that for rehashing dicts, that is, in the case of safe iterators
   178	 * and Scan, we won't delete the dict. We will check whether it needs
   179	 * to be deleted when we're releasing the iterator. */
   180	static void freeDictIfNeeded(kvstore *kvs, int didx) {
   181	    if (!(kvs->flags & KVSTORE_FREE_EMPTY_DICTS) ||
   182	        !kvstoreGetDict(kvs, didx) ||
   183	        kvstoreDictSize(kvs, didx) != 0 ||
   184	        kvstoreDictIsRehashingPaused(kvs, didx))
   185	        return;
   186	    dictRelease(kvs->dicts[didx]);
   187	    kvs->dicts[didx] = NULL;
   188	    kvs->allocated_dicts--;
   189	}
   190	
   191	/**********************************/
   192	/*** dict callbacks ***************/
   193	/**********************************/
   194	
   195	/* Adds dictionary to the rehashing list, which allows us
   196	 * to quickly find rehash targets during incremental rehashing.
   197	 *
   198	 * If there are multiple dicts, updates the bucket count for the given dictionary
   199	 * in a DB, bucket count incremented with the new ht size during the rehashing phase.
   200	 * If there's one dict, bucket count can be retrieved directly from single dict bucket. */
   201	static void kvstoreDictRehashingStarted(dict *d) {
   202	    kvstore *kvs = d->type->userdata;
   203	    kvstoreDictMetaBase *metadata = (kvstoreDictMetaBase *)dictMetadata(d);
   204	    listAddNodeTail(kvs->rehashing, d);
   205	    metadata->rehashing_node = listLast(kvs->rehashing);
   206	
   207	    unsigned long long from, to;
   208	    dictRehashingInfo(d, &from, &to);
   209	    kvs->overhead_hashtable_rehashing += from;
   210	}
   211	
   212	/* Remove dictionary from the rehashing list.
   213	 *
   214	 * Updates the bucket count for the given dictionary in a DB. It removes
   215	 * the old ht size of the dictionary from the total sum of buckets for a DB.  */
   216	static void kvstoreDictRehashingCompleted(dict *d) {
   217	    kvstore *kvs = d->type->userdata;
   218	    kvstoreDictMetaBase *metadata = (kvstoreDictMetaBase *)dictMetadata(d);
   219	    if (metadata->rehashing_node) {
   220	        listDelNode(kvs->rehashing, metadata->rehashing_node);
   221	        metadata->rehashing_node = NULL;
   222	    }
   223	
   224	    unsigned long long from, to;
   225	    dictRehashingInfo(d, &from, &to);
   226	    kvs->overhead_hashtable_rehashing -= from;
   227	}
   228	
   229	/* Updates the bucket count for the given dictionary in a DB. It adds the new ht size
   230	 * of the dictionary or removes the old ht size of the dictionary from the total
   231	 * sum of buckets for a DB. */
   232	static void kvstoreDictBucketChanged(dict *d, long long delta) {
   233	    kvstore *kvs = d->type->userdata;
   234	    kvs->bucket_count += delta;
   235	}
   236	
   237	/* Returns the size of the DB dict base metadata in bytes. */
   238	static size_t kvstoreDictMetaBaseSize(dict *d) {
   239	    UNUSED(d);
   240	    return sizeof(kvstoreDictMetaBase);
   241	}
   242	/* Returns the size of the DB dict extended metadata in bytes. */
   243	static size_t kvstoreDictMetadataExtendSize(dict *d) {
   244	    UNUSED(d);
   245	    return sizeof(kvstoreDictMetaEx);
   246	}
   247	
   248	/**********************************/
   249	/*** API **************************/
   250	/**********************************/
   251	
   252	/* Create an array of dictionaries
   253	 * num_dicts_bits is the log2 of the amount of dictionaries needed (e.g. 0 for 1 dict,
   254	 * 3 for 8 dicts, etc.) */
   255	kvstore *kvstoreCreate(dictType *type, int num_dicts_bits, int flags) {
   256	    /* We can't support more than 2^16 dicts because we want to save 48 bits
   257	     * for the dict cursor, see kvstoreScan */
   258	    assert(num_dicts_bits <= 16);
   259	
   260	    /* Calc kvstore size */   
   261	    size_t kvsize = sizeof(kvstore);
   262	    /* Conditionally calc also histogram size */
   263	    if (flags & KVSTORE_ALLOC_META_KEYS_HIST) 
   264	        kvsize += sizeof(kvstoreMetadata);
   265	    
   266	    kvstore *kvs = zcalloc(kvsize);
   267	    memcpy(&kvs->dtype, type, sizeof(kvs->dtype));
   268	    kvs->flags = flags;
   269	
   270	    /* kvstore must be the one to set these callbacks, so we make sure the
   271	     * caller didn't do it */
   272	    assert(!type->userdata);
   273	    assert(!type->dictMetadataBytes);
   274	    assert(!type->rehashingStarted);
   275	    assert(!type->rehashingCompleted);
   276	    kvs->dtype.userdata = kvs;
   277	    if (flags & KVSTORE_ALLOC_META_KEYS_HIST)
   278	        kvs->dtype.dictMetadataBytes = kvstoreDictMetadataExtendSize;
   279	    else
   280	        kvs->dtype.dictMetadataBytes = kvstoreDictMetaBaseSize;
   281	    kvs->dtype.rehashingStarted = kvstoreDictRehashingStarted;
   282	    kvs->dtype.rehashingCompleted = kvstoreDictRehashingCompleted;
   283	    kvs->dtype.bucketChanged = kvstoreDictBucketChanged;
   284	
   285	    kvs->num_dicts_bits = num_dicts_bits;
   286	    kvs->num_dicts = 1 << kvs->num_dicts_bits;
   287	    kvs->dicts = zcalloc(sizeof(dict*) * kvs->num_dicts);
   288	    if (!(kvs->flags & KVSTORE_ALLOCATE_DICTS_ON_DEMAND)) {
   289	        for (int i = 0; i < kvs->num_dicts; i++)
   290	            createDictIfNeeded(kvs, i);
   291	    }
   292	
   293	    kvs->rehashing = listCreate();
   294	    kvs->key_count = 0;
   295	    kvs->non_empty_dicts = 0;
   296	    kvs->resize_cursor = 0;
   297	    kvs->dict_size_index = kvs->num_dicts > 1? zcalloc(sizeof(unsigned long long) * (kvs->num_dicts + 1)) : NULL;
   298	    kvs->bucket_count = 0;
   299	    kvs->overhead_hashtable_rehashing = 0;
   300	    return kvs;
   301	}
   302	
   303	void kvstoreEmpty(kvstore *kvs, void(callback)(dict*)) {
   304	    for (int didx = 0; didx < kvs->num_dicts; didx++) {
   305	        dict *d = kvstoreGetDict(kvs, didx);
   306	        if (!d)
   307	            continue;
   308	        kvstoreDictMetaBase *metadata = (kvstoreDictMetaBase *)dictMetadata(d);
   309	        if (metadata->rehashing_node)
   310	            metadata->rehashing_node = NULL;
   311	        if (kvs->flags & KVSTORE_ALLOC_META_KEYS_HIST) {
   312	            kvstoreDictMetaEx *metaExt = (kvstoreDictMetaEx *) metadata;
   313	            memset(&metaExt->meta.keysizes_hist, 0, sizeof(metaExt->meta.keysizes_hist));
   314	        }
   315	        dictEmpty(d, callback);
   316	        freeDictIfNeeded(kvs, didx);
   317	    }
   318	
   319	    if (kvs->flags & KVSTORE_ALLOC_META_KEYS_HIST)
   320	        memset(kvstoreGetMetadata(kvs), 0, sizeof(kvstoreMetadata));
   321	
   322	    listEmpty(kvs->rehashing);
   323	
   324	    kvs->key_count = 0;
   325	    kvs->non_empty_dicts = 0;
   326	    kvs->resize_cursor = 0;
   327	    kvs->bucket_count = 0;
   328	    if (kvs->dict_size_index)
   329	        memset(kvs->dict_size_index, 0, sizeof(unsigned long long) * (kvs->num_dicts + 1));
   330	    kvs->overhead_hashtable_rehashing = 0;
   331	}
   332	
   333	void kvstoreRelease(kvstore *kvs) {
   334	    for (int didx = 0; didx < kvs->num_dicts; didx++) {
   335	        dict *d = kvstoreGetDict(kvs, didx);
   336	        if (!d)
   337	            continue;
   338	        kvstoreDictMetaBase *metadata = (kvstoreDictMetaBase *)dictMetadata(d);
   339	        if (metadata->rehashing_node)
   340	            metadata->rehashing_node = NULL;
   341	        dictRelease(d);
   342	    }
   343	    zfree(kvs->dicts);
   344	
   345	    listRelease(kvs->rehashing);
   346	    if (kvs->dict_size_index)
   347	        zfree(kvs->dict_size_index);
   348	
   349	    zfree(kvs);
   350	}
   351	
   352	unsigned long long int kvstoreSize(kvstore *kvs) {
   353	    if (kvs->num_dicts != 1) {
   354	        return kvs->key_count;
   355	    } else {
   356	        return kvs->dicts[0]? dictSize(kvs->dicts[0]) : 0;
   357	    }
   358	}
   359	
   360	/* This method provides the cumulative sum of all the dictionary buckets
   361	 * across dictionaries in a database. */
   362	unsigned long kvstoreBuckets(kvstore *kvs) {
   363	    if (kvs->num_dicts != 1) {
   364	        return kvs->bucket_count;
   365	    } else {
   366	        return kvs->dicts[0]? dictBuckets(kvs->dicts[0]) : 0;
   367	    }
   368	}
   369	
   370	size_t kvstoreMemUsage(kvstore *kvs) {
   371	    size_t mem = sizeof(*kvs);
   372	    size_t metaSize = sizeof(kvstoreDictMetaBase);
   373	
   374	    if (kvs->flags & KVSTORE_ALLOC_META_KEYS_HIST)
   375	        metaSize = sizeof(kvstoreDictMetaEx);
   376	    
   377	    unsigned long long keys_count = kvstoreSize(kvs);
   378	    mem += keys_count * dictEntryMemUsage(kvs->dtype.no_value) +
   379	           kvstoreBuckets(kvs) * sizeof(dictEntry*) +
   380	           kvs->allocated_dicts * (sizeof(dict) + metaSize);
   381	
   382	    /* Values are dict* shared with kvs->dicts */
   383	    mem += listLength(kvs->rehashing) * sizeof(listNode);
   384	
   385	    return mem;
   386	}
   387	
   388	/*
   389	 * This method is used to iterate over the elements of the entire kvstore specifically across dicts.
   390	 * It's a three pronged approach.
   391	 *
   392	 * 1. It uses the provided cursor `cursor` to retrieve the dict index from it.
   393	 * 2. If the dictionary is in a valid state checked through the provided callback `dictScanValidFunction`,
   394	 *    it performs a dictScan over the appropriate `keyType` dictionary of `db`.
   395	 * 3. If the dict is entirely scanned i.e. the cursor has reached 0, the next non empty dict is discovered.
   396	 *    The dict information is embedded into the cursor and returned.
   397	 *
   398	 * To restrict the scan to a single dict, pass a valid dict index as
   399	 * 'onlydidx', otherwise pass -1.
   400	 */
   401	unsigned long long kvstoreScan(kvstore *kvs, unsigned long long cursor,
   402	                               int onlydidx, dictScanFunction *scan_cb,
   403	                               kvstoreScanShouldSkipDict *skip_cb,
   404	                               void *privdata)
   405	{
   406	    unsigned long long _cursor = 0;
   407	    /* During dictionary traversal, 48 upper bits in the cursor are used for positioning in the HT.
   408	     * Following lower bits are used for the dict index number, ranging from 0 to 2^num_dicts_bits-1.
   409	     * Dict index is always 0 at the start of iteration and can be incremented only if there are
   410	     * multiple dicts. */
   411	    int didx = getAndClearDictIndexFromCursor(kvs, &cursor);
   412	    if (onlydidx >= 0) {
   413	        if (didx < onlydidx) {
   414	            /* Fast-forward to onlydidx. */
   415	            assert(onlydidx < kvs->num_dicts);
   416	            didx = onlydidx;
   417	            cursor = 0;
   418	        } else if (didx > onlydidx) {
   419	            /* The cursor is already past onlydidx. */
   420	            return 0;
   421	        }
   422	    }
   423	
   424	    dict *d = kvstoreGetDict(kvs, didx);
   425	
   426	    int skip = !d || (skip_cb && skip_cb(d));
   427	    if (!skip) {
   428	        _cursor = dictScan(d, cursor, scan_cb, privdata);
   429	        /* In dictScan, scan_cb may delete entries (e.g., in active expire case). */
   430	        freeDictIfNeeded(kvs, didx);
   431	    }
   432	    /* scanning done for the current dictionary or if the scanning wasn't possible, move to the next dict index. */
   433	    if (_cursor == 0 || skip) {
   434	        if (onlydidx >= 0)
   435	            return 0;
   436	        didx = kvstoreGetNe<response clipped><NOTE>To save on context only part of this file has been shown to you. You should retry this tool after you have searched inside the file with `grep -n` in order to find the line numbers of what you are looking for.</NOTE>

    31	/* Using dictSetResizeEnabled() we make possible to disable
    32	 * resizing and rehashing of the hash table as needed. This is very important
    33	 * for Redis, as we use copy-on-write and don't want to move too much memory
    34	 * around when there is a child performing saving operations.
    35	 *
    36	 * Note that even when dict_can_resize is set to DICT_RESIZE_AVOID, not all
    37	 * resizes are prevented:
    38	 *  - A hash table is still allowed to expand if the ratio between the number
    39	 *    of elements and the buckets >= dict_force_resize_ratio.
    40	 *  - A hash table is still allowed to shrink if the ratio between the number
    41	 *    of elements and the buckets <= 1 / (HASHTABLE_MIN_FILL * dict_force_resize_ratio). */
    42	static dictResizeEnable dict_can_resize = DICT_RESIZE_ENABLE;

   123	/* --------------------- dictEntry pointer bit tricks ----------------------  */
   124	
   125	/* The 3 least significant bits in a pointer to a dictEntry determines what the
   126	 * pointer actually points to. If the least bit is set, it's a key. Otherwise,
   127	 * the bit pattern of the least 3 significant bits mark the kind of entry. */
   128	
   129	#define ENTRY_PTR_MASK        7 /* 111 */
   130	#define ENTRY_PTR_NORMAL      0 /* 000 : If a pointer to an entry with value. */
   131	#define ENTRY_PTR_IS_ODD_KEY  1 /* XX1 : If a pointer to odd key address (must be 1). */
   132	#define ENTRY_PTR_IS_EVEN_KEY 2 /* 010 : If a pointer to even key address. (must be 2 or 4). */ 
   133	#define ENTRY_PTR_NO_VALUE    4 /* 100 : If a pointer to an entry without value. */ 
   134	
   135	/* Returns 1 if the entry pointer is a pointer to a key, rather than to an
   136	 * allocated entry. Returns 0 otherwise. */
   137	static inline int entryIsKey(const dictEntry *de) {
   138	    return ((uintptr_t)de & (ENTRY_PTR_IS_ODD_KEY | ENTRY_PTR_IS_EVEN_KEY));
   139	}
   140	
   141	/* Returns 1 if the pointer is actually a pointer to a dictEntry struct. Returns
   142	 * 0 otherwise. */
   143	static inline int entryIsNormal(const dictEntry *de) {
   144	    return ((uintptr_t)(void *)de & ENTRY_PTR_MASK) == ENTRY_PTR_NORMAL;
   145	}
   146	
   147	/* Returns 1 if the entry is a special entry with key and next, but without
   148	 * value. Returns 0 otherwise. */
   149	static inline int entryIsNoValue(const dictEntry *de) {
   150	    return ((uintptr_t)(void *)de & ENTRY_PTR_MASK) == ENTRY_PTR_NO_VALUE;
   151	}
   152	
   153	/* Creates an entry without a value field. */
   154	static inline dictEntry *createEntryNoValue(void *key, dictEntry *next) {
   155	    dictEntryNoValue *entry = zmalloc(sizeof(*entry));
   156	    entry->key = key;
   157	    entry->next = next;
   158	    return (dictEntry *)(void *)((uintptr_t)(void *)entry | ENTRY_PTR_NO_VALUE);
   159	}
   160	
   161	static inline dictEntry *encodeMaskedPtr(const void *ptr, unsigned int bits) {
   162	    assert(((uintptr_t)ptr & ENTRY_PTR_MASK) == 0);
   163	    return (dictEntry *)(void *)((uintptr_t)ptr | bits);
   164	}
   165	
   166	static inline void *decodeMaskedPtr(const dictEntry *de) {
   167	    return (void *)((uintptr_t)(void *)de & ~ENTRY_PTR_MASK);
   168	}
   169	
   170	/* Decodes the pointer to an entry without value, when you know it is an entry
   171	 * without value. Hint: Use entryIsNoValue to check. */
   172	static inline dictEntryNoValue *decodeEntryNoValue(const dictEntry *de) {
   173	    return decodeMaskedPtr(de);
   174	}
   175	
   176	/* Returns 1 if the entry has a value field and 0 otherwise. */
   177	static inline int entryHasValue(const dictEntry *de) {
   178	    return entryIsNormal(de);
   179	}
   180	
   181	/* ----------------------------- API implementation ------------------------- */
   182	
   183	/* Reset hash table parameters already initialized with _dictInit()*/
   184	static void _dictReset(dict *d, int htidx)
   185	{
   186	    d->ht_table[htidx] = NULL;
   187	    d->ht_size_exp[htidx] = -1;
   188	    d->ht_used[htidx] = 0;
   189	}
   190	
   191	/* Create a new hash table */
   192	dict *dictCreate(dictType *type)
   193	{
   194	    size_t metasize = type->dictMetadataBytes ? type->dictMetadataBytes(NULL) : 0;
   195	    dict *d = zmalloc(sizeof(*d)+metasize);
   196	    if (metasize > 0) {
   197	        memset(dictMetadata(d), 0, metasize);
   198	    }
   199	    _dictInit(d,type);
   200	    return d;
   201	}
   202	
   203	/* Change dictType of dict to another one with metadata support
   204	 * Rest of dictType's values must stay the same */
   205	void dictTypeAddMeta(dict **d, dictType *typeWithMeta) {
   206	    /* Verify new dictType is compatible with the old one */
   207	    dictType toCmp = *typeWithMeta;
   208	    toCmp.dictMetadataBytes = NULL;                            /* Expected old one not to have metadata */
   209	    toCmp.onDictRelease = (*d)->type->onDictRelease;           /* Ignore 'onDictRelease' in comparison */
   210	    assert(memcmp((*d)->type, &toCmp, sizeof(dictType)) == 0); /* The rest of the dictType fields must be the same */
   211	
   212	    *d = zrealloc(*d, sizeof(dict) + typeWithMeta->dictMetadataBytes(*d));
   213	    (*d)->type = typeWithMeta;
   214	}
   215	
   216	/* Initialize the hash table */
   217	int _dictInit(dict *d, dictType *type)
   218	{
   219	    _dictReset(d, 0);
   220	    _dictReset(d, 1);
   221	    d->type = type;
   222	    d->rehashidx = -1;
   223	    d->pauserehash = 0;
   224	    d->pauseAutoResize = 0;
   225	    d->useStoredKeyApi = 0;
   226	    return DICT_OK;
   227	}
   228	
   229	/* Resize or create the hash table,
   230	 * when malloc_failed is non-NULL, it'll avoid panic if malloc fails (in which case it'll be set to 1).
   231	 * Returns DICT_OK if resize was performed, and DICT_ERR if skipped. */
   232	int _dictResize(dict *d, unsigned long size, int* malloc_failed)
   233	{
   234	    if (malloc_failed) *malloc_failed = 0;
   235	
   236	    /* We can't rehash twice if rehashing is ongoing. */
   237	    assert(!dictIsRehashing(d));
   238	
   239	    /* the new hash table */
   240	    dictEntry **new_ht_table;
   241	    unsigned long new_ht_used;
   242	    signed char new_ht_size_exp = _dictNextExp(size);
   243	
   244	    /* Detect overflows */
   245	    size_t newsize = DICTHT_SIZE(new_ht_size_exp);
   246	    if (newsize < size || newsize * sizeof(dictEntry*) < newsize)
   247	        return DICT_ERR;
   248	
   249	    /* Rehashing to the same table size is not useful. */
   250	    if (new_ht_size_exp == d->ht_size_exp[0]) return DICT_ERR;
   251	
   252	    /* Allocate the new hash table and initialize all pointers to NULL */
   253	    if (malloc_failed) {
   254	        new_ht_table = ztrycalloc(newsize*sizeof(dictEntry*));
   255	        *malloc_failed = new_ht_table == NULL;
   256	        if (*malloc_failed)
   257	            return DICT_ERR;
   258	    } else
   259	        new_ht_table = zcalloc(newsize*sizeof(dictEntry*));
   260	
   261	    new_ht_used = 0;
   262	
   263	    /* Prepare a second hash table for incremental rehashing.
   264	     * We do this even for the first initialization, so that we can trigger the
   265	     * rehashingStarted more conveniently, we will clean it up right after. */
   266	    d->ht_size_exp[1] = new_ht_size_exp;
   267	    d->ht_used[1] = new_ht_used;
   268	    d->ht_table[1] = new_ht_table;
   269	    d->rehashidx = 0;
   270	    if (d->type->rehashingStarted) d->type->rehashingStarted(d);
   271	    if (d->type->bucketChanged)
   272	        d->type->bucketChanged(d, DICTHT_SIZE(d->ht_size_exp[1]));
   273	
   274	    /* Is this the first initialization or is the first hash table empty? If so
   275	     * it's not really a rehashing, we can just set the first hash table so that
   276	     * it can accept keys. */
   277	    if (d->ht_table[0] == NULL || d->ht_used[0] == 0) {
   278	        if (d->type->rehashingCompleted) d->type->rehashingCompleted(d);
   279	        if (d->type->bucketChanged)
   280	            d->type->bucketChanged(d, -(long long)DICTHT_SIZE(d->ht_size_exp[0]));
   281	        if (d->ht_table[0]) zfree(d->ht_table[0]);
   282	        d->ht_size_exp[0] = new_ht_size_exp;
   283	        d->ht_used[0] = new_ht_used;
   284	        d->ht_table[0] = new_ht_table;
   285	        _dictReset(d, 1);
   286	        d->rehashidx = -1;
   287	        return DICT_OK;
   288	    }
   289	
   290	    /* Force a full rehashing of the dictionary */
   291	    if (d->type->force_full_rehash) {
   292	        while (dictRehash(d, 1000)) {
   293	            /* Continue rehashing */
   294	        }
   295	    }
   296	    return DICT_OK;
   297	}
   298	
   299	int _dictExpand(dict *d, unsigned long size, int* malloc_failed) {
   300	    /* the size is invalid if it is smaller than the size of the hash table 
   301	     * or smaller than the number of elements already inside the hash table */
   302	    if (dictIsRehashing(d) || d->ht_used[0] > size || DICTHT_SIZE(d->ht_size_exp[0]) >= size)
   303	        return DICT_ERR;
   304	    return _dictResize(d, size, malloc_failed);
   305	}
   306	
   307	/* return DICT_ERR if expand was not performed */
   308	int dictExpand(dict *d, unsigned long size) {
   309	    return _dictExpand(d, size, NULL);
   310	}
   311	
   312	/* return DICT_ERR if expand failed due to memory allocation failure */
   313	int dictTryExpand(dict *d, unsigned long size) {
   314	    int malloc_failed = 0;
   315	    _dictExpand(d, size, &malloc_failed);
   316	    return malloc_failed? DICT_ERR : DICT_OK;
   317	}
   318	
   319	/* return DICT_ERR if shrink was not performed */
   320	int dictShrink(dict *d, unsigned long size) {
   321	    /* the size is invalid if it is bigger than the size of the hash table
   322	     * or smaller than the number of elements already inside the hash table */
   323	    if (dictIsRehashing(d) || d->ht_used[0] > size || DICTHT_SIZE(d->ht_size_exp[0]) <= size)
   324	        return DICT_ERR;
   325	    return _dictResize(d, size, NULL);
   326	}
   327	
   328	/* Helper function for `dictRehash` and `dictBucketRehash` which rehashes all the keys
   329	 * in a bucket at index `idx` from the old to the new hash HT. */
   330	static void rehashEntriesInBucketAtIndex(dict *d, uint64_t idx) {
   331	    dictEntry *de = d->ht_table[0][idx];
   332	    uint64_t h;
   333	    dictEntry *nextde;
   334	    while (de) {
   335	        nextde = dictGetNext(de);
   336	        void *key = dictGetKey(de);
   337	        /* Get the index in the new hash table */
   338	        if (d->ht_size_exp[1] > d->ht_size_exp[0]) {
   339	            h = dictHashKey(d, key, 1) & DICTHT_SIZE_MASK(d->ht_size_exp[1]);
   340	        } else {
   341	            /* We're shrinking the table. The tables sizes are powers of
   342	             * two, so we simply mask the bucket index in the larger table
   343	             * to get the bucket index in the smaller table. */
   344	            h = idx & DICTHT_SIZE_MASK(d->ht_size_exp[1]);
   345	        }
   346	        if (d->type->no_value) {
   347	            if (!d->ht_table[1][h]) {
   348	                /* The destination bucket is empty, allowing the key to be stored 
   349	                 * directly without allocating a dictEntry. If an old entry was 
   350	                 * previously allocated, free its memory. */                
   351	                if (!entryIsKey(de)) zfree(decodeMaskedPtr(de));
   352	                
   353	                if (d->type->keys_are_odd)
   354	                    de = key; /* ENTRY_PTR_IS_ODD_KEY trivially set by the odd key. */
   355	                else
   356	                    de = encodeMaskedPtr(key, ENTRY_PTR_IS_EVEN_KEY);
   357	                
   358	            } else if (entryIsKey(de)) {
   359	                /* We don't have an allocated entry but we need one. */
   360	                de = createEntryNoValue(key, d->ht_table[1][h]);
   361	            } else {
   362	                /* Just move the existing entry to the destination table and
   363	                 * update the 'next' field. */
   364	                assert(entryIsNoValue(de));
   365	                dictSetNext(de, d->ht_table[1][h]);
   366	            }
   367	        } else {
   368	            dictSetNext(de, d->ht_table[1][h]);
   369	        }
   370	        d->ht_table[1][h] = de;
   371	        d->ht_used[0]--;
   372	        d->ht_used[1]++;
   373	        de = nextde;
   374	    }
   375	    d->ht_table[0][idx] = NULL;
   376	}
   377	
   378	/* This checks if we already rehashed the whole table and if more rehashing is required */
   379	static int dictCheckRehashingCompleted(dict *d) {
   380	    if (d->ht_used[0] != 0) return 0;
   381	    
   382	    if (d->type->rehashingCompleted) d->type->rehashingCompleted(d);
   383	    if (d->type->bucketChanged)
   384	        d->type->bucketChanged(d, -(long long)DICTHT_SIZE(d->ht_size_exp[0]));
   385	    zfree(d->ht_table[0]);
   386	    /* Copy the new ht onto the old one */
   387	    d->ht_table[0] = d->ht_table[1];
   388	    d->ht_used[0] = d->ht_used[1];
   389	    d->ht_size_exp[0] = d->ht_size_exp[1];
   390	    _dictReset(d, 1);
   391	    d->rehashidx = -1;
   392	    return 1;
   393	}
   394	
   395	/* Performs N steps of incremental rehashing. Returns 1 if there are still
   396	 * keys to move from the old to the new hash table, otherwise 0 is returned.
   397	 *
   398	 * Note that a rehashing step consists in moving a bucket (that may have more
   399	 * than one key as we use chaining) from the old to the new hash table, however
   400	 * since part of the hash table may be composed of empty spaces, it is not
   401	 * guaranteed that this function will rehash even a single bucket, since it
   402	 * will visit at max N*10 empty buckets in total, otherwise the amount of
   403	 * work it does would be unbound and the function may block for a long time. */
   404	int dictRehash(dict *d, int n) {
   405	    int empty_visits = n*10; /* Max number of empty buckets to visit. */
   406	    unsigned long s0 = DICTHT_SIZE(d->ht_size_exp[0]);
   407	    unsigned long s1 = DICTHT_SIZE(d->ht_size_exp[1]);
   408	    if (dict_can_resize == DICT_R<response clipped><NOTE>To save on context only part of this file has been shown to you. You should retry this tool after you have searched inside the file with `grep -n` in order to find the line numbers of what you are looking for.</NOTE>

  1714	static signed char _dictNextExp(unsigned long size)
  1715	{
  1716	    if (size <= DICT_HT_INITIAL_SIZE) return DICT_HT_INITIAL_EXP;
  1717	    if (size >= LONG_MAX) return (8*sizeof(long)-1);
  1718	
  1719	    return 8*sizeof(long) - __builtin_clzl(size-1);

  1722	/* Finds and returns the link within the dict where the provided key should
  1723	 * be inserted using dictInsertKeyAtLink() if the key does not already exist in
  1724	 * the dict. If the key exists in the dict, NULL is returned and the optional
  1725	 * 'existing' entry pointer is populated, if provided. */
  1726	dictEntryLink dictFindLinkForInsert(dict *d, const void *key, dictEntry **existing) {
  1727	    unsigned long idx, table;
  1728	    dictCmpCache cmpCache = {0};
  1729	    dictEntry *he;
  1730	    uint64_t hash = dictHashKey(d, key, d->useStoredKeyApi);
  1731	    if (existing) *existing = NULL;
  1732	    idx = hash & DICTHT_SIZE_MASK(d->ht_size_exp[0]);
  1733	
  1734	    /* Rehash the hash table if needed */
  1735	    _dictRehashStepIfNeeded(d,idx);
  1736	
  1737	    /* Expand the hash table if needed */
  1738	    _dictExpandIfNeeded(d);
  1739	    keyCmpFunc cmpFunc = dictGetCmpFunc(d);
  1740	
  1741	    for (table = 0; table <= 1; table++) {
  1742	        if (table == 0 && (long)idx < d->rehashidx) continue; 
  1743	        idx = hash & DICTHT_SIZE_MASK(d->ht_size_exp[table]);
  1744	        /* Search if this slot does not already contain the given key */
  1745	        he = d->ht_table[table][idx];
  1746	        while(he) {
  1747	            void *he_key = dictGetKey(he);
  1748	            if (key == he_key || cmpFunc(&cmpCache, key, he_key)) {
  1749	                if (existing) *existing = he;
  1750	                return NULL;
  1751	            }
  1752	            he = dictGetNext(he);
  1753	        }
  1754	        if (!dictIsRehashing(d)) break;
  1755	    }
  1756	
  1757	    /* If we are in the process of rehashing the hash table, the bucket is
  1758	     * always returned in the context of the second (new) hash table. */
  1759	    dictEntry **bucket = &d->ht_table[dictIsRehashing(d) ? 1 : 0][idx];
  1760	    return bucket;
  1761	}

   712	int _dictClear(dict *d, int htidx, void(callback)(dict*)) {
   713	    unsigned long i;
   714	
   715	    /* Free all the elements */
   716	    for (i = 0; i < DICTHT_SIZE(d->ht_size_exp[htidx]) && d->ht_used[htidx] > 0; i++) {
   717	        dictEntry *he, *nextHe;
   718	        /* Callback will be called once for every 65535 deletions. Beware,
   719	         * if dict has less than 65535 items, it will not be called at all.*/
   720	        if (callback && i != 0 && (i & 65535) == 0) callback(d);
   721	
   722	        if ((he = d->ht_table[htidx][i]) == NULL) continue;
   723	        while(he) {
   724	            nextHe = dictGetNext(he);
   725	            dictFreeKey(d, he);
   726	            dictFreeVal(d, he);
   727	            if (!entryIsKey(he)) zfree(decodeMaskedPtr(he));
   728	            d->ht_used[htidx]--;
   729	            he = nextHe;
   730	        }
   731	    }
   732	    /* Free the table and the allocated cache structure */
   733	    zfree(d->ht_table[htidx]);
   734	    /* Re-initialize the table */
   735	    _dictReset(d, htidx);
   736	    return DICT_OK; /* never fails */
   737	}
   738	
   739	/* Clear & Release the hash table */
   740	void dictRelease(dict *d)
   741	{
   742	    /* Someone may be monitoring a dict that started rehashing, before
   743	     * destroying the dict fake completion. */
   744	    if (dictIsRehashing(d) && d->type->rehashingCompleted)
   745	        d->type->rehashingCompleted(d);
   746	
   747	    /* Subtract the size of all buckets. */
   748	    if (d->type->bucketChanged)
   749	        d->type->bucketChanged(d, -(long long)dictBuckets(d));
   750	
   751	    if (d->type->onDictRelease)
   752	        d->type->onDictRelease(d);
   753	
   754	    _dictClear(d,0,NULL);
   755	    _dictClear(d,1,NULL);
   756	    zfree(d);
   757	}

   810	 * may not be the server main DBs (could be a temporary DB).
   811	 *
   812	 * The dbnum can be -1 if all the DBs should be emptied, or the specified
   813	 * DB index if we want to empty only a single database.
   814	 * The function returns the number of keys removed from the database(s). */
   815	long long emptyDbStructure(redisDb *dbarray, int dbnum, int async,
   816	                           void(callback)(dict*))
   817	{
   818	    long long removed = 0;
   819	    int startdb, enddb;
   820	
   821	    if (dbnum == -1) {
   822	        startdb = 0;
   823	        enddb = server.dbnum-1;
   824	    } else {
   825	        startdb = enddb = dbnum;
   826	    }
   827	
   828	    for (int j = startdb; j <= enddb; j++) {
   829	        removed += kvstoreSize(dbarray[j].keys);
   830	        if (async) {
   831	            emptyDbAsync(&dbarray[j]);
   832	        } else {
   833	            /* Destroy global HFE DS before deleting the hashes since ebuckets
   834	             * DS is embedded in the stored objects. */
   835	            ebDestroy(&dbarray[j].hexpires, &hashExpireBucketsType, NULL);
   836	            kvstoreEmpty(dbarray[j].keys, callback);
   837	            kvstoreEmpty(dbarray[j].expires, callback);
   838	        }
   839	        /* Because all keys of database are removed, reset average ttl. */
   840	        dbarray[j].avg_ttl = 0;
   841	        dbarray[j].expires_cursor = 0;
   842	    }
   843	
   844	    return removed;
   845	}
   846	
   847	/* Remove all data (keys and functions) from all the databases in a
   848	 * Redis server. If callback is given the function is called from
   849	 * time to time to signal that work is in progress.
   850	 *
   851	 * The dbnum can be -1 if all the DBs should be flushed, or the specified
   852	 * DB number if we want to flush only a single Redis database number.
   853	 *
   854	 * Flags are be EMPTYDB_NO_FLAGS if no special flags are specified or
   855	 * EMPTYDB_ASYNC if we want the memory to be freed in a different thread
   856	 * and the function to return ASAP. EMPTYDB_NOFUNCTIONS can also be set
   857	 * to specify that we do not want to delete the functions.
   858	 *
   859	 * On success the function returns the number of keys removed from the
   860	 * database(s). Otherwise -1 is returned in the specific case the
   861	 * DB number is out of range, and errno is set to EINVAL. */
   862	long long emptyData(int dbnum, int flags, void(callback)(dict*)) {
   863	    int async = (flags & EMPTYDB_ASYNC);
   864	    int with_functions = !(flags & EMPTYDB_NOFUNCTIONS);
   865	    RedisModuleFlushInfoV1 fi = {REDISMODULE_FLUSHINFO_VERSION,!async,dbnum};
   866	    long long removed = 0;
   867	
   868	    if (dbnum < -1 || dbnum >= server.dbnum) {
   869	        errno = EINVAL;
   870	        return -1;
   871	    }
   872	
   873	    /* Fire the flushdb modules event. */
   874	    moduleFireServerEvent(REDISMODULE_EVENT_FLUSHDB,
   875	                          REDISMODULE_SUBEVENT_FLUSHDB_START,
   876	                          &fi);
   877	
   878	    /* Make sure the WATCHed keys are affected by the FLUSH* commands.
   879	     * Note that we need to call the function while the keys are still
   880	     * there. */
   881	    signalFlushedDb(dbnum, async);
   882	
   883	    /* Empty redis database structure. */
   884	    removed = emptyDbStructure(server.db, dbnum, async, callback);
   885	
   886	    if (dbnum == -1) flushSlaveKeysWithExpireList();
   887	
   888	    if (with_functions) {
   889	        serverAssert(dbnum == -1);
   890	        functionsLibCtxClearCurrent(async);
   891	    }
   892	
   893	    /* Also fire the end event. Note that this event will fire almost
   894	     * immediately after the start event if the flush is asynchronous. */
   895	    moduleFireServerEvent(REDISMODULE_EVENT_FLUSHDB,
   896	                          REDISMODULE_SUBEVENT_FLUSHDB_END,
   897	                          &fi);
   898	
   899	    return removed;
   900	}
   901	
   902	/* Initialize temporary db on replica for use during diskless replication. */
   903	redisDb *initTempDb(void) {
   904	    int slot_count_bits = 0;
   905	    int flags = KVSTORE_ALLOCATE_DICTS_ON_DEMAND;
   906	    if (server.cluster_enabled) {
   907	        slot_count_bits = CLUSTER_SLOT_MASK_BITS;
   908	        flags |= KVSTORE_FREE_EMPTY_DICTS;
   909	    }
   910	    redisDb *tempDb = zcalloc(sizeof(redisDb)*server.dbnum);
   911	    for (int i=0; i<server.dbnum; i++) {
   912	        tempDb[i].id = i;
   913	        tempDb[i].keys = kvstoreCreate(&dbDictType, slot_count_bits,
   914	                                       flags | KVSTORE_ALLOC_META_KEYS_HIST);
   915	        tempDb[i].expires = kvstoreCreate(&dbExpiresDictType, slot_count_bits, flags);
   916	        tempDb[i].hexpires = ebCreate();
   917	    }

   198	/* Empty a Redis DB asynchronously. What the function does actually is to
   199	 * create a new empty set of hash tables and scheduling the old ones for
   200	 * lazy freeing. */
   201	void emptyDbAsync(redisDb *db) {
   202	    int slot_count_bits = 0;
   203	    int flags = KVSTORE_ALLOCATE_DICTS_ON_DEMAND;
   204	    if (server.cluster_enabled) {
   205	        slot_count_bits = CLUSTER_SLOT_MASK_BITS;
   206	        flags |= KVSTORE_FREE_EMPTY_DICTS;
   207	    }
   208	    kvstore *oldkeys = db->keys, *oldexpires = db->expires;
   209	    ebuckets oldHfe = db->hexpires;
   210	    db->keys = kvstoreCreate(&dbDictType, slot_count_bits, flags | KVSTORE_ALLOC_META_KEYS_HIST);
   211	    db->expires = kvstoreCreate(&dbExpiresDictType, slot_count_bits, flags);
   212	    db->hexpires = ebCreate();
   213	    atomicIncr(lazyfree_objects, kvstoreSize(oldkeys));
   214	    bioCreateLazyFreeJob(lazyfreeFreeDatabase, 3, oldkeys, oldexpires, oldHfe);
   215	}

So default is 0 (not lazy). So it's using `EMPTYDB_NO_FLAGS`, which means `async` is 0, and it goes through the sync path: `kvstoreEmpty`.

Now let me look at `kvstoreEmpty`:

```c
void kvstoreEmpty(kvstore *kvs, void(callback)(dict*)) {
    for (int didx = 0; didx < kvs->num_dicts; didx++) {
        dict *d = kvstoreGetDict(kvs, didx);
        if (!d)
            continue;
        kvstoreDictMetaBase *metadata = (kvstoreDictMetaBase *)dictMetadata(d);
        if (metadata->rehashing_node)
            metadata->rehashing_node = NULL;
        if (kvs->flags & KVSTORE_ALLOC_META_KEYS_HIST) {
            kvstoreDictMetaEx *metaExt = (kvstoreDictMetaEx *) metadata;
            memset(&metaExt->meta.keysizes_hist, 0, sizeof(metaExt->meta.keysizes_hist));
        }
        dictEmpty(d, callback);
        freeDictIfNeeded(kvs, didx);
    }
    ...
}
```

Now `dictEmpty` -> `_dictClear`. But wait, what if the dict is rehashing? The `dictEmpty` function calls `rehashingCompleted` callback first. Let me look at what `rehashingCompleted` does for kvstore:

```c
static void kvstoreDictRehashingCompleted(dict *d) {
    kvstore *kvs = d->type->userdata;
    kvstoreDictMetaBase *metadata = (kvstoreDictMetaBase *)dictMetadata(d);
    if (metadata->rehashing_node) {
        listDelNode(kvs->rehashing, metadata->rehashing_node);
        metadata->rehashing_node = NULL;
    }

    unsigned long long from, to;
    dictRehashingInfo(d, &from, &to);
    kvs->overhead_hashtable_rehashing -= from;
}
```

And then `dictEmpty` does:

```c
void dictEmpty(dict *d, void(callback)(dict*)) {
    if (dictIsRehashing(d) && d->type->rehashingCompleted)
        d->type->rehashingCompleted(d);

    if (d->type->bucketChanged)
        d->type->bucketChanged(d, -(long long)dictBuckets(d));

    _dictClear(d,0,callback);
    _dictClear(d,1,callback);
    d->rehashidx = -1;
    d->pauserehash = 0;
    d->pauseAutoResize = 0;
}
```

Wait, but the issue is: what if `_dictClear` with `htidx=0` also frees some dict entries, and one of those entries has a NULL key? How would a NULL key get in there?

Let me think about this differently. Let me look at the `kvstoreEmpty` function and how it interacts with `freeDictIfNeeded`. After `dictEmpty` is called, `freeDictIfNeeded` is called:

```c
static void freeDictIfNeeded(kvstore *kvs, int didx) {
    if (!(kvs->flags & KVSTORE_FREE_EMPTY_DICTS) ||
        !kvstoreGetDict(kvs, didx) ||
        kvstoreDictSize(kvs, didx) != 0 ||
        kvstoreDictIsRehashingPaused(kvs, didx))
        return;
    dictRelease(kvs->dicts[didx]);
    kvs->dicts[didx] = NULL;
    kvs->allocated_dicts--;
}
```

But the key question is: what if a dict has entries that are stored directly as keys (the no-value case)? In that case, `entryIsKey` returns true, and `dictGetKey` might return something odd.

Actually, let me look at this more carefully. The `dbDictType` is used:

Actually, this is getting complicated. Let me focus on the actual bug instead. Let me look at the PR description again: "Redis 8.0.2 slave keep crashing when it startup."

Let me look at the `kvstoreEmpty` function more carefully. The issue might be that when `kvstoreEmpty` is called and there's a rehashing dict, something goes wrong with the metadata.

Wait, let me look at the `kvstoreDictRehashingCompleted` callback:

```c
static void kvstoreDictRehashingCompleted(dict *d) {
    kvstore *kvs = d->type->userdata;
    kvstoreDictMetaBase *metadata = (kvstoreDictMetaBase *)dictMetadata(d);
    if (metadata->rehashing_node) {
        listDelNode(kvs->rehashing, metadata->rehashing_node);
        metadata->rehashing_node = NULL;
    }

    unsigned long long from, to;
    dictRehashingInfo(d, &from, &to);
    kvs->overhead_hashtable_rehashing -= from;
}
```

And `dictEmpty`:

```c
void dictEmpty(dict *d, void(callback)(dict*)) {
    if (dictIsRehashing(d) && d->type->rehashingCompleted)
        d->type->rehashingCompleted(d);

    if (d->type->bucketChanged)
        d->type->bucketChanged(d, -(long long)dictBuckets(d));

    _dictClear(d,0,callback);
    _dictClear(d,1,callback);
    d->rehashidx = -1;
    d->pauserehash = 0;
    d->pauseAutoResize = 0;
}
```

And then `kvstoreEmpty` after calling `dictEmpty`:

```c
void kvstoreEmpty(kvstore *kvs, void(callback)(dict*)) {
    for (int didx = 0; didx < kvs->num_dicts; didx++) {
        dict *d = kvstoreGetDict(kvs, didx);
        if (!d)
            continue;
        kvstoreDictMetaBase *metadata = (kvstoreDictMetaBase *)dictMetadata(d);
        if (metadata->rehashing_node)
            metadata->rehashing_node = NULL;
        if (kvs->flags & KVSTORE_ALLOC_META_KEYS_HIST) {
            kvstoreDictMetaEx *metaExt = (kvstoreDictMetaEx *) metadata;
            memset(&metaExt->meta.keysizes_hist, 0, sizeof(metaExt->meta.keysizes_hist));
        }
        dictEmpty(d, callback);
        freeDictIfNeeded(kvs, didx);
    }
    ...
}
```

After `dictEmpty`, the dict is empty but not freed (unless `KVSTORE_FREE_EMPTY_DICTS` is set). But wait, `freeDictIfNeeded` checks:
```c
static void freeDictIfNeeded(kvstore *kvs, int didx) {
    if (!(kvs->flags & KVSTORE_FREE_EMPTY_DICTS) ||
        !kvstoreGetDict(kvs, didx) ||
        kvstoreDictSize(kvs, didx) != 0 ||
        kvstoreDictIsRehashingPaused(kvs, didx))
        return;
    dictRelease(kvs->dicts[didx]);
    kvs->dicts[didx] = NULL;
    kvs->allocated_dicts--;
}
```

For the main DB kvstore (created with `KVSTORE_ALLOCATE_DICTS_ON_DEMAND` but not `KVSTORE_FREE_EMPTY_DICTS`), the dict is NOT freed after emptying.

Now, let me think about the RDB loading scenario on a slave. The slave receives a full RDB, loads it, and during that process:
1. `rdbLoadEmptyDbFunc` is called
2. `emptyData(-1, ...)` is called
3. The callback `replicationEmptyDbCallback` calls `processEventsWhileBlocked()`

Is it possible that during `processEventsWhileBlocked()`, some module or other code gets executed that modifies state in a way that corrupts things?

OK, so these are all regular dicts, not kvstores. None of them should be affected by `emptyDbStructure`.

Let me look at the problem from the RDB loading perspective. Maybe the issue is with `kvstoreEmpty` being called when the dict has entries with no-value representation (where the key itself is stored as the entry pointer). Let me look at how entries are added to the db dicts:

The db dicts have `no_value = 1` and `keys_are_odd = 0`. So entries are stored as `encodeMaskedPtr(key, ENTRY_PTR_IS_EVEN_KEY)`. When `_dictClear` processes these entries:

```c
while(he) {
    nextHe = dictGetNext(he);
    dictFreeKey(d, he);   // -> dictDestructorKV(d, dictGetKey(he))
    dictFreeVal(d, he);   // valDestructor is NULL for dbDictType, so nothing
    if (!entryIsKey(he)) zfree(decodeMaskedPtr(he));
    d->ht_used[htidx]--;
    he = nextHe;
}
```

For `dbDictType`, entries are keys (pointers with `ENTRY_PTR_IS_EVEN_KEY` bit set). `entryIsKey` returns true. So `!entryIsKey(he)` is false, and we don't free. `dictGetKey` returns `decodeMaskedPtr(he)` which is the actual robj pointer. `dictDestructorKV` decrements refcount.

But what about `dbExpiresDictType`? It has `keyDestructor = NULL`, so `dictFreeKey` does nothing. `valDestructor = NULL`. But wait, `dbExpiresDictType` also has `no_value = 1` and `keys_are_odd = 0`, so entries are stored as encoded pointers.

Actually, let me look at the `expire` dict more carefully. The `dbExpiresDictType` has `keyDestructor = NULL`. So when clearing, keys are NOT freed. But the keys in the expire dict are the same pointers as in the keys dict. That should be fine - the keys dict will free them.

But wait - what if there's a bug where the expire dict has an entry whose key was already freed? That could cause a use-after-free. But that would crash at `dictGetKey`, not at `dictSdsDestructor`.

2026-05-29 08:50:46,328 - DEBUG - swea-tools - Retrieved state from environment: {'working_dir': '/testbed'}

commit f9530e77d108f4d46da3aaef0b8a3792688f2fc6
Author: debing.sun <debing.sun@redis.com>
Date:   Wed May 7 16:45:23 2025 +0800

    Correctly update kvstore overhead after emptying or releasing dict (#13984)
    
    Close #13973
    
    This PR fixed two bugs.
    1)  `overhead_hashtable_lut` isn't updated correctly
        This bug was introduced by https://github.com/redis/redis/pull/12913
    We only update `overhead_hashtable_lut` at the beginning and end of
    rehashing, but we forgot to update it when a dict is emptied or
    released.
    
    This PR introduces a new `bucketChanged` callback to track the change
    changes in the bucket size.
    Now, `rehashingStarted` and `rehashingCompleted` callbacks are no longer
    responsible for bucket changes, but are entirely handled by
    `bucketChanged`, this can also avoid that we need to register three
    callbacks to track the change of bucket size, now only one is needed.
    
    In most cases, it will be triggered together with `rehashingStarted` or
    `rehashingCompleted`,
    except when a dict is being emptied or released, in these cases, even if
    the dict is not rehashing, we still need to subtract its current size.
    
    On the other hand, `overhead_hashtable_lut` was duplicated with
    `bucket_count`, so we remove `overhead_hashtable_lut` and use
    `bucket_count` instead.
    
    Note that this bug only happens with cluster mode, because we don't use
    KVSTORE_FREE_EMPTY_DICTS without cluster.
    
    2) The size of `dict_size_index` repeatedly counted in terms of memory
    usage.
    `dict_size_index` is created at startup, so its memory usage has been
    counted into `used_memory_startup`.
    However, when we want to count the overhead, we repeat the calculation,
    which may cause the overhead to exceed the total memory usage.
    
    ---------
    
    Co-authored-by: Yuan Wang <yuan.wang@redis.com>

                           void(callback)(dict*))

The callback is `replicationEmptyDbCallback`. This is called from `_dictClear`. Let me look at `_dictClear` again:

```c
int _dictClear(dict *d, int htidx, void(callback)(dict*)) {
    unsigned long i;
    for (i = 0; i < DICTHT_SIZE(d->ht_size_exp[htidx]) && d->ht_used[htidx] > 0; i++) {
        dictEntry *he, *nextHe;
        if (callback && i != 0 && (i & 65535) == 0) callback(d);
        if ((he = d->ht_table[htidx][i]) == NULL) continue;
        while(he) {
            nextHe = dictGetNext(he);
            dictFreeKey(d, he);
            dictFreeVal(d, he);
            if (!entryIsKey(he)) zfree(decodeMaskedPtr(he));
            d->ht_used[htidx]--;
            he = nextHe;
        }
    }
    ...
}
```

The callback is called every 65535 buckets. So during this process, `processEventsWhileBlocked()` gets called. That can trigger all sorts of processing.

Hmm, but what about the `dictSdsDestructor`? Let me check if maybe the `KVSTORE_ALLOC_META_KEYS_HIST` flag causes something. Let me look at what `kvstoreEmpty` does before `dictEmpty`:

```c
void kvstoreEmpty(kvstore *kvs, void(callback)(dict*)) {
    for (int didx = 0; didx < kvs->num_dicts; didx++) {
        dict *d = kvstoreGetDict(kvs, didx);
        if (!d)
            continue;
        kvstoreDictMetaBase *metadata = (kvstoreDictMetaBase *)dictMetadata(d);
        if (metadata->rehashing_node)
            metadata->rehashing_node = NULL;
        if (kvs->flags & KVSTORE_ALLOC_META_KEYS_HIST) {
            kvstoreDictMetaEx *metaExt = (kvstoreDictMetaEx *) metadata;
            memset(&metaExt->meta.keysizes_hist, 0, sizeof(metaExt->meta.keysizes_hist));
        }
        dictEmpty(d, callback);
        freeDictIfNeeded(kvs, didx);
    }
    ...
}
```

The `metadata->rehashing_node` could be non-NULL if the dict was rehashing. Setting it to NULL is fine, but later when `dictEmpty` calls `d->type->rehashingCompleted(d)`, the `kvstoreDictRehashingCompleted` callback will try to do:

```c
static void kvstoreDictRehashingCompleted(dict *d) {
    kvstore *kvs = d->type->userdata;
    kvstoreDictMetaBase *metadata = (kvstoreDictMetaBase *)dictMetadata(d);
    if (metadata->rehashing_node) {
        listDelNode(kvs->rehashing, metadata->rehashing_node);
        metadata->rehashing_node = NULL;
    }
    ...
}
```

Since `kvstoreEmpty` already cleared `metadata->rehashing_node`, `listDelNode` won't be called. So that's fine.

Wait, but what about `listDelNode`? If `rehashing_node` was already cleared, then `metadata->rehashing_node` will be NULL and we skip. But what if the list `kvs->rehashing` already had that node removed? Let me check...

Actually, there's a potential issue: `kvstoreEmpty` sets `metadata->rehashing_node = NULL` BEFORE calling `dictEmpty`. Then `dictEmpty` calls `kvstoreDictRehashingCompleted` which tries to check `metadata->rehashing_node` - it's NULL, so it skips the `listDelNode`. But the node is still in the list! Then later `listEmpty(kvs->rehashing)` is called, which should remove all nodes. But the `listEmpty` function might just free the list without cleaning up nodes properly?

So RSI contains what looks like a string pointer. But this is a weird address: `0x5f726f7461726570`. This is NOT a typical heap address (heap addresses usually look like `0x7f...` or `0x55...`). This looks like the string data was somehow written into the pointer itself!

Wait! `5f726f7461726570` - that's 8 ASCII characters! `_rotarep` = `perator_` reversed. This is actually string data, not a pointer. Something has corrupted the dict entry, replacing the key pointer with the key content itself.

This could be a memory corruption issue. But let me think about what could cause this...

Actually, wait. In the dict with `no_value=1`, entries can be stored as encoded pointers. For `dbDictType`, `keys_are_odd = 0`, so entries use `ENTRY_PTR_IS_EVEN_KEY`. But `dictSdsDestructor` is NOT used by `dbDictType`.

```c
long long emptyDbStructure(redisDb *dbarray, int dbnum, int async,
                           void(callback)(dict*))
{
    ...
    for (int j = startdb; j <= enddb; j++) {
        removed += kvstoreSize(dbarray[j].keys);

            emptyDbAsync(&dbarray[j]);
        } else {
            ebDestroy(&dbarray[j].hexpires, &hashExpireBucketsType, NULL);
            kvstoreEmpty(dbarray[j].keys, callback);
            kvstoreEmpty(dbarray[j].expires, callback);
        }

```

The `kvstoreEmpty(dbarray[j].keys, callback)` clears the main keys dict. The `dbDictType` has `dictDestructorKV` as key destructor:

```c
static void dictDestructorKV(dict *d, void *kv) {
    UNUSED(d);
    if (kv == NULL) return;
    decrRefCount(kv);
}
```

When `decrRefCount` is called on a robj that is a set, it will decrement the refcount. If it reaches 0, `freeSetObject` or similar is called, which might call `dictRelease` on the set's internal dict, which uses `setDictType` with `dictSdsDestructor`. 

So the path could be:
1. `kvstoreEmpty` → `dictEmpty` → `_dictClear` → `dictFreeKey` → `dictDestructorKV` → `decrRefCount(kvobj)`
2. Refcount reaches 0 → object is freed → set dict is released → `dictSdsDestructor` is called on set elements

But the crash is at `dictSdsDestructor` with what looks like a corrupted sds string. The value `0x5f726f7461726570` ("perator_") is suspicious - it looks like part of a string but it's stored where a pointer should be.

Hmm, but this is the normal object destruction path. The set dict should have valid sds strings.

Wait, actually let me look at where `dictRelease` calls `_dictClear`:

```c
void dictRelease(dict *d)
{
    if (dictIsRehashing(d) && d->type->rehashingCompleted)
        d->type->rehashingCompleted(d);
    if (d->type->bucketChanged)
        d->type->bucketChanged(d, -(long long)dictBuckets(d));
    if (d->type->onDictRelease)
        d->type->onDictRelease(d);
    _dictClear(d,0,NULL);
    _dictClear(d,1,NULL);
    zfree(d);
}
```

And `_dictClear`:
```c
int _dictClear(dict *d, int htidx, void(callback)(dict*)) {
    ...
    while(he) {
        nextHe = dictGetNext(he);
        dictFreeKey(d, he);
        dictFreeVal(d, he);
        if (!entryIsKey(he)) zfree(decodeMaskedPtr(he));
        d->ht_used[htidx]--;
        he = nextHe;
    }
    ...
}
```

For `setDictType`, `no_value = 1` and `keys_are_odd = 1`. When the entry is stored as an encoded key (since `keys_are_odd = 1`, and sds pointers are odd), `entryIsKey(he)` returns true. So `dictGetKey(he)` returns `(void *)he` (the pointer itself, since `ENTRY_PTR_IS_ODD_KEY` is set). Then `dictFreeKey` calls `dictSdsDestructor(d, (void *)he)`.

But wait! If the entry is stored as an odd key, the key IS the pointer itself (with bit 0 set). But `dictSdsDestructor` calls `sdsfree(val)`. But `val` is not a real sds string - it's the dict entry pointer with bit 0 set! That would be a corrupted pointer!

Hold on, let me re-check `dictGetKey`:

```c
void *dictGetKey(const dictEntry *de) {
    /* if entryIsKey() */
    if ((uintptr_t)de & ENTRY_PTR_IS_ODD_KEY) return (void *) de;
    if ((uintptr_t)de & ENTRY_PTR_IS_EVEN_KEY) return decodeMaskedPtr(de);    
    /* Regular entry */ 
    if (entryIsNoValue(de)) return decodeEntryNoValue(de)->key;
    return de->key;
}
```

For `keys_are_odd = 1`, when an sds key is stored, it's stored as the key pointer itself (with bit 0 set implicitly because sds pointers are odd on some architectures? No, actually, sds pointers are NOT guaranteed to be odd. The comment says "an SDS string is always an odd pointer" - but that's only true if the allocator returns odd-aligned pointers for sds strings, which is not always the case.

Wait, let me re-read the code path for inserting a key when `keys_are_odd = 1`:

In `dict.c` line ~353:
```c
if (d->type->keys_are_odd)
    de = key; /* ENTRY_PTR_IS_ODD_KEY trivially set by the odd key. */
```

So the assumption is that the key pointer itself has bit 0 set (odd). But if the key is an sds string that happens to have an even address, this would be wrong!

Actually, for `keys_are_odd = 1`, the key is used directly as the entry pointer. The key must have bit 0 set (be an odd address). For sds strings allocated by jemalloc, addresses might not always be odd. But the code assumes they are.

But this is a pre-existing design, not a bug introduced by this PR.

Let me look at the `rehashEntriesInBucketAtIndex` function in dict.c:

```c
static void rehashEntriesInBucketAtIndex(dict *d, uint64_t idx) {
    dictEntry *de = d->ht_table[0][idx];
    uint64_t h;
    dictEntry *nextde;
    while (de) {
        nextde = dictGetNext(de);
        void *key = dictGetKey(de);
        /* Get the index in the new hash table */
        if (d->ht_size_exp[1] > d->ht_size_exp[0]) {
            h = dictHashKey(d, key, 1) & DICTHT_SIZE_MASK(d->ht_size_exp[1]);
        } else {
            h = idx & DICTHT_SIZE_MASK(d->ht_size_exp[1]);
        }
        if (d->type->no_value) {
            if (!d->ht_table[1][h]) {
                if (!entryIsKey(de)) zfree(decodeMaskedPtr(de));
                if (d->type->keys_are_odd)
                    de = key; /* ENTRY_PTR_IS_ODD_KEY trivially set by the odd key. */
                else
                    de = encodeMaskedPtr(key, ENTRY_PTR_IS_EVEN_KEY);
            } else if (entryIsKey(de)) {
                de = createEntryNoValue(key, d->ht_table[1][h]);
            } else {
                assert(entryIsNoValue(de));
                dictSetNext(de, d->ht_table[1][h]);
            }
        } else {
            dictSetNext(de, d->ht_table[1][h]);
        }
        d->ht_table[1][h] = de;
        d->ht_used[0]--;
        d->ht_used[1]++;
        de = nextde;
    }
    d->ht_table[0][idx] = NULL;
}
```

There's a critical issue here! When `keys_are_odd` is true and the destination bucket is empty:
```c
if (d->type->keys_are_odd)
    de = key; /* ENTRY_PTR_IS_ODD_KEY trivially set by the odd key. */
```

This sets `de` to `key` (which is the raw key pointer). But then:
```c
d->ht_table[1][h] = de;
```

The entry `de` is now just the key pointer (with assumed odd bit set). But `dictGetKey` for an odd pointer returns `(void *)de` - which is the key itself. That works.

But what if the key is NOT odd? The comment says "an SDS string is always an odd pointer" but that might not be guaranteed. If an sds string happens to be allocated at an even address, then the `keys_are_odd` optimization would break.

But this is a long-standing design issue, not specific to this crash.

Actually, let me reconsider. Maybe the issue is simpler. Let me look at `dictDestructorKV`:

When `decrRefCount` is called on an object, it might free the object. If the object is a set, `freeSetObject` is called, which calls `dictRelease` on the set's internal dict. This `dictRelease` calls `_dictClear` on the set dict, which calls `dictSdsDestructor` for each sds key.

But wait - the set's dict uses `setDictType` which has `keys_are_odd = 1` and `no_value = 1`. In `_dictClear`:

```c
while(he) {
    nextHe = dictGetNext(he);

    ...

```

For `keys_are_odd = 1`, `entryIsKey(he)` checks `((uintptr_t)de & (ENTRY_PTR_IS_ODD_KEY | ENTRY_PTR_IS_EVEN_KEY))`. Since `ENTRY_PTR_IS_ODD_KEY = 1`, this returns true if bit 0 is set. For an sds pointer that's odd, this is true. Then `dictGetKey(he)` returns `(void *) he` (the pointer itself with bit 0 set). But wait - `dictGetKey` returns `(void *) de` for odd entries. But `de` has bit 0 set (because it's the key pointer with the odd bit). So `dictGetKey` returns a value with bit 0 set. That value is then passed to `dictSdsDestructor` which calls `sdsfree(val)`.

But `sdsfree` expects a valid sds pointer! A valid sds pointer points to the string data (after the header). If the key is an sds string and it's stored directly as the entry (with bit 0 set), then `dictGetKey` returns the sds pointer with bit 0 set. But then `sdsfree` would try to interpret this pointer with bit 0 set, which would read from the wrong memory location!

Wait, let me check: `sdsfree(s)` checks `if (s == NULL) return;` then reads `s[-1]`. If `s` has bit 0 set, then `s[-1]` reads from `(s & ~1) - 1`, which might still work but would read the wrong byte. Actually, `s[-1]` with bit 0 set would read from `s - 1`, which might be misaligned and read garbage.

But this is how the `keys_are_odd` optimization works. For `setDictType`, `keys_are_odd = 1` because sds pointers are supposed to be odd. The sds pointer itself (pointing to string data) should have bit 0 set because the sds header is at an even address and the data follows at an odd address (or vice versa).

Actually, I think I understand now. sds strings are allocated with `s_malloc` which returns pointers aligned to some boundary. The sds header is placed before the string data. If the header size is odd, then the string data pointer would be odd. Let me check:

`sds` allocates memory for header + string + 1 (null terminator). The header size depends on the type. The pointer to the string data is `(char*)ptr + hdrlen`. If the allocated pointer is 8-byte aligned (jemalloc), and the header size is odd, then the string data pointer would be odd.

The sds header types:
- SDS_TYPE_5: 1 byte header (unused)
- SDS_TYPE_8: 3 bytes header (len:1, alloc:1, flags:1)
- SDS_TYPE_16: 5 bytes header
- SDS_TYPE_32: 9 bytes header
- SDS_TYPE_64: 17 bytes header

So SDS_TYPE_8 (3 bytes) would make the data pointer at offset +3 from the allocation, which would be odd if the allocation is even. Similarly SDS_TYPE_32 (9 bytes) at offset +9 would be odd. But SDS_TYPE_16 (5 bytes) at offset +5 would be odd. SDS_TYPE_64 (17 bytes) at offset +17 would be odd.

BUT: if the allocator returns a pointer that's 8-byte aligned (0 mod 8), then:
- +3 → 3 mod 8 → odd ✓ (SDS_TYPE_8)
- +5 → 5 mod 8 → odd ✓ (SDS_TYPE_16)
- +9 → 1 mod 8 → odd ✓ (SDS_TYPE_32)
- +17 → 1 mod 8 → odd ✓ (SDS_TYPE_64)

So yes, sds pointers should always be odd given 8-byte aligned allocation. So the `keys_are_odd` optimization is valid.

OK, so `dictGetKey` for odd entries returns `(void *)de` which is the sds pointer with bit 0 set (which is how sds pointers naturally are). Then `dictSdsDestructor` calls `sdsfree(val)` where `val` is this sds pointer. `sdsfree` reads `s[-1]` which is the flags byte. For an odd sds pointer, `s[-1]` is the byte just before the string data, which is the last byte of the sds header (flags byte). This is correct.

So the `keys_are_odd` optimization is valid for sds. And the crash is not due to this.

Let me now look at the actual hexdump more carefully. The instruction at `dictSdsDestructor+0x8` is `movzbl -0x1(%rsi), %eax`. The value of RSI from the register dump is `0x5f726f7461726570`. This is NOT a valid sds pointer. It looks like string data.

This suggests that the dict entry being freed has a corrupted key. The question is: how did the dict entry get corrupted?

Let me look at the `emptyDbStructure` path again. When we call `kvstoreEmpty(dbarray[j].keys, callback)`, the dict type is `dbDictType`:

```c
dictType dbDictType = {
    dictSdsHash,            /* hash function */
    NULL,                   /* key dup */
    NULL,                   /* val dup */
    dictSdsCompareKV,       /* lookup key compare */
    dictDestructorKV,       /* key destructor */
    NULL,                   /* val destructor */
    dictResizeAllowed,      /* allow to resize */
    .no_value = 1,          /* keys and values are unified (kvobj) */
    .keys_are_odd = 0,      /* simple kvobj (robj) struct */
    .storedHashFunction = dictHashKV,  /* stored hash function */
    .storedKeyCompare = dictCompareKV, /* stored key compare */
};
```

Key destructor is `dictDestructorKV`, NOT `dictSdsDestructor`. So the crash is NOT from the main db dict!

So where is the crash coming from? It must be from a nested dict. When `dictDestructorKV` is called on a robj, it decrements the refcount. If the robj is a set or hash or zset, its internal dict might be freed. The internal dict of a set uses `setDictType` which has `dictSdsDestructor`.

So the path is:
1. `kvstoreEmpty` on `db->keys` calls `dictEmpty`
2. `_dictClear` frees each key (robj) via `dictDestructorKV` → `decrRefCount`
3. If robj is a set, `freeSetObject` → `dictRelease` on set's internal dict
4. Set's internal dict uses `setDictType` → `dictSdsDestructor` for each element
5. One of the set elements is corrupted → crash

But how would a set element be corrupted? Unless there's memory corruption from elsewhere.

Wait, could the issue be related to the `hexpires` (hash expiration buckets)? Let me look at the `ebDestroy` call:

```c
ebDestroy(&dbarray[j].hexpires, &hashExpireBucketsType, NULL);
```

This destroys the hash expiration buckets before clearing the dicts. The hash expiration buckets contain references to hash objects. If `ebDestroy` frees something that the dict still references, we might get use-after-free.

Let me look at `ebDestroy`:

The `onDeleteItem` is NULL for `hashExpireBucketsType`, so `ebDestroy` just marks items as trash and doesn't free them. The actual hash objects are freed when the main dict is cleared (via `decrRefCount` on each key).

OK, I'm spending too much time tracing the wrong path. Let me look at this from a higher level.

The PR description says this is a crash on Redis 8.0.2 slave. The crash is at `dictSdsDestructor`. The crash log says "Flushing old data" right before the crash. The slave has `repl-diskless-load disabled`.

Let me look at what's special about the slave startup path. When a slave starts up and does a full resync, it:
1. Receives the RDB from the master
2. Saves it to disk (since diskless-load is disabled)
3. Calls `rdbLoadWithEmptyFunc` which calls `rdbLoadEmptyDbFunc`
4. `rdbLoadEmptyDbFunc` calls `emptyData(-1, ...)` which flushes the existing DB
5. Then loads the RDB

But wait, the slave is just starting up. Why would it have existing data to flush? Unless it had a previous partial sync that left some data?

Actually, looking at the log:
```
1027239:S 12 Aug 2025 10:40:39.502 * Full resync from master: 403f5eadaf40b46fa5a90ccde54b462606b52604:15123965342078
```

This is a FULL resync, not a partial one. The slave receives a full RDB. Before loading, it flushes old data.

Hmm, but if the slave is just starting up fresh, `emptyData` would iterate over empty dicts and do nothing. Unless the slave had some data from a previous run (like an RDB file that was loaded at startup before replication starts).

Wait, that's it! The slave starts up, loads its own RDB/AOF, then connects to the master. When the master responds with a full resync, the slave needs to flush its existing data before loading the master's RDB. So the slave has data that needs to be flushed.

Now, the crash happens during the flush. And the crash is in `dictSdsDestructor` with what looks like corrupted data. This suggests memory corruption that happened earlier, maybe during the initial local RDB load.

But the PR description says "slave keep crashing when it startup" - meaning it crashes every time at the same place. So it's reproducible.

Let me look at this from yet another angle. Maybe the issue is that `dictSdsDestructor` needs a NULL check, just like `dictObjectDestructor` and `dictDestructorKV` have. The hexdump of the crashed binary shows that `dictSdsDestructor` HAS a NULL check (the `test rsi, rsi; je`). But wait - the hexdump might be showing the inlined `sdsfree` function, and the NULL check is inside `sdsfree`, not in `dictSdsDestructor` itself.

If `dictSdsDestructor` called `sdsfree(val)` and `sdsfree` checks for NULL, then the NULL check is there. But the hexdump at `dictSdsDestructor` shows the inlined body of `sdsfree`, including the NULL check. So the NULL check IS present.

But the crash still happens. The issue must be that the value being passed is not NULL but a corrupted pointer that happens to look like a valid pointer but points to invalid memory.

Let me check: RSI = `0x5f726f7461726570`. This is a large address, not NULL. `sdsfree` would read `s[-1]` at `0x5f726f746172656f`. If that address is not mapped, we get SIGSEGV. And indeed, the crash says "Accessing address: (nil)" - but wait, the address being accessed is `0x5f726f746172656f`, not nil.

Unless the kernel reports the faulting address as nil because the address calculation wrapped around? No, `0x5f726f7461726570 - 1 = 0x5f726f746172656f`, which doesn't wrap.

OK, I think the "Accessing address: (nil)" might be misleading or from a different instruction. Let me just focus on the fix.

Given that `dictSdsDestructor` can be called with a value that might be corrupt, adding a NULL check won't help because the value isn't NULL. But adding a NULL check is still good practice for consistency with other destructors.

But more importantly, I need to understand WHY the corruption happens. Let me look at this commit that might be related:

```
2af69a931 Do not call _dictClear()'s callback for the first 65k items (#13674)
```

commit 2af69a931ab45aad22204763bf93e1050629eede
Author: Ozan Tezcan <ozantezcan@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Dec 3 09:26:19 2024 +0300

    Do not call _dictClear()'s callback for the first 65k items (#13674)
    
    In https://github.com/redis/redis/pull/13495, we introduced a feature to
    reply -LOADING while flushing a large db on a replica.
    While `_dictClear()` is in progress, it calls a callback for every 65k
    items and we yield back to eventloop to reply -LOADING.
    
    This change has made some tests unstable as those tests don't expect new
    -LOADING reply.
    One observation, inside `_dictClear()`, we call the callback even if db
    has a few keys. Most tests run with small amount of keys. So, each
    replication and cluster test has to handle potential -LOADING reply now.
    
    This PR changes this behavior, skips calling callback when `i=0` to
    stabilize replication tests.
    Callback will be called after the first 65k items. Most tests use less
    than 65k keys and they won't get -LOADING reply.

commit a7afd1d2b2b0b9b64c44fd950d57e49ad8823bde
Author: Ozan Tezcan <ozantezcan@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Sep 3 09:48:44 2024 +0300

    Reply LOADING on replica while flushing the db (#13495)
    
    On a full sync, replica starts discarding existing db. If the existing
    db is huge and flush is happening synchronously, replica may become
    unresponsive.
    
    Adding a change to yield back to event loop while flushing db on
    a replica. Replica will reply -LOADING in this case. Note that while
    replica is loading the new rdb, it may get an error and start flushing
    the partial db. This step may take a long time as well. Similarly,
    replica will reply -LOADING in this case.
    
    To call processEventsWhileBlocked() and reply -LOADING, we need to do:
    - Set connSetReadHandler() null not to process further data from the master
    - Set server.loading flag
    - Call blockingOperationStarts()
    
    rdbload() already does these steps and calls processEventsWhileBlocked()
    while loading the rdb. Added a new call rdbLoadWithEmptyFunc() which
    accepts callback to flush db before loading rdb or when an error
    happens while loading.
    
    For diskless replication, doing something similar and calling emptyData()
    after setting required flags.
    
    Additional changes:
    - Allow `appendonly` config change during loading.
     Config can be changed while loading data on startup or on replication
     when slave is loading RDB. We allow config change command to update
     `server.aof_enabled` and then lazily apply config change after loading
     operation is completed.
    
     - Added a test for `replica-lazy-flush` config
